  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c058c4cc-cf2a-4fb8-8286-c941fdf1ee9b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText2016139740832020786" style="display:none">Theodosia was six when her country was invaded and her mother, the Fire Queen, was murdered before her eyes. On that day, the Kaiser took Theodosia's family, her land, and her name. Theo was crowned Ash Princess--a title of shame to bear in her new life as a prisoner.<br /><br />For ten years Theo has been a captive in her own palace. She's endured the relentless abuse and ridicule of the Kaiser and his court. She is powerless, surviving in her new world only by burying the girl she was deep inside.<br /><br />Then, one night, the Kaiser forces her to do the unthinkable. With blood on her hands and all hope of reclaiming her throne lost, she realizes that surviving is no longer enough. But she does have a weapon: her mind is sharper than any sword. And power isn't always won on the battlefield.<br /><br />For ten years, the Ash Princess has seen her land pillaged and her people enslaved. That all ends here.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1318551-besides-portraying-violence-in-the-form-of">Besides portraying violence in the form of &#39;brutal whippings&#39;, does this book include rape? What are the trigger warnings?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1318551'><a id="like_count_community_question_1318551" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1318551?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">9 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F32505753-ash-princess">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1318551-besides-portraying-violence-in-the-form-of">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1318551-besides-portraying-violence-in-the-form-of">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5345628-laura"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1502725847i/5345628._UY100_CR24,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5345628-laura">Laura</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi! I've actually been getting this question a lot and I did a Twitter thread about it. I'm compiling it here so it can be easily found.<br/><br/>"Hey y’all. I’<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi! I've actually been getting this question a lot and I did a Twitter thread about it. I'm compiling it here so it can be easily found.<br /><br />"Hey y’all. I’m seeing some discussion of the violence in Ash Princess so I want to talk a bit about that so that readers can go in with open eyes. AKA here are some trigger warnings. I’m going to try to be vague enough to avoid spoilers, but there may be some very light ones.<br /><br />Ash Princess is about a conquered country where the original inhabitants are all slaves. About half of the main cast of characters are or were slaves and they talk very frankly about their experiences, including being beaten, starved, and raped.<br /><br />To be clear: there is no on-page rape or attempted rape in the book. The discussions of it happening off-page aren’t graphic or explicit.<br /><br />One of my biggest pet peeves in storytelling is when rape is used as a plot device. I didn’t want to do that here. But at the same time, it would have been been disingenuous to write about colonization without including it.<br /><br />Though there isn’t on-page rape, there are some scenes where the unspoken threat of it hangs over Theo’s head. There are scenes with uninvited and inappropriate touching.<br /><br />There is also physical and psychological abuse including one graphic whipping scene. Again, this kind of violence was not something I set out to write and, in all honesty, they were the hardest scenes for me. But again, I felt they were necessary.<br /><br />Theo’s world is an ugly one and I found its roots in real history. Not including the violent aspects and the ripples created by them would have been, I felt, to gloss over the atrocities of war and colonization that persist to this day in our very real world.<br /><br />However, the last thing I want to do is to blindside people who already understand that all too well. If anyone has any questions about this, please feel free to reach out to me through DMs."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127095204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18129317990361328122"><blockquote>
  <i>Is it better to have your life ended by someone who hates you or someone who loves you?</i>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32505753.Ash_Princess' title='Ash Princess by Laura Sebastian' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ash Princess</a> has a heroine desperately trying to reclaim her stolen throne, a mindlessly evil tyrant who stole said throne, and a love triangle... What's that, you say? You've heard this one before? Yeah, me too. <br/><br/>That being said, to give credit where it's due, it stands out for being <b>compulsively readable and entertaining</b>.<br/><br/>Plot and character-wise, it resembles many other YA fantasies. But I was just complai</span>
  <span id="freeText18129317990361328122" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Is it better to have your life ended by someone who hates you or someone who loves you?</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32505753.Ash_Princess" title="Ash Princess by Laura Sebastian" rel="nofollow noopener">Ash Princess</a> has a heroine desperately trying to reclaim her stolen throne, a mindlessly evil tyrant who stole said throne, and a love triangle... What's that, you say? You've heard this one before? Yeah, me too. <br /><br />That being said, to give credit where it's due, it stands out for being <b>compulsively readable and entertaining</b>.<br /><br />Plot and character-wise, it resembles many other YA fantasies. But I was just complaining in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34726469.Sky_in_the_Deep" title="Sky in the Deep by Adrienne Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Sky in the Deep</a> about how I keep reading a lot of “shallow and emotionless” YA fantasy books, and this happens to be one that breaks the pattern. I can't deny it is very compelling, though it relies heavily on violence, abuse and misery to keep us turning the pages.<br /><br />I'll spare you a plot summary - you can probably guess it anyway - and just say there's a rightful queen held captive by the conquerors of her kingdom who must assist the underground rebellion and reclaim her throne. Whilst fighting off the hot dudes along the way, of course.<br /><br />Many are comparing this to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>, which I did think was shallow and emotionless. Instead, I’d compare it to Sabaa Tahir’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a> - both books are heavy on the violence, feature slavery as a theme, have a love triangle (sort of) and an evil tyrant driving the drama and action. They are also similarly paced and engaging. <br /><br />Aside from an awkward infodump in the first chapter, it goes down smoothly. The violence and unfairness make it easy to keep turning the pages. Shortly after the book opens Theo is forced to murder her father, and <b>nothing gets me reading like a nice dose of fury at the injustice of it all</b>. Theo's undercover manipulations are also fun to read.<br /><br />Some of the major plot aspects seem illogical, such as why the new king (called the Kaiser 🙄) would leave the rightful heir alive. The book tries to explain it away but it doesn't really make much sense. Surely if you want to dampen any hope of reinstating the rightful monarch then you would just kill the rightful monarch.<br /><br />I should warn that it is at times grim and gory. Slavery is a norm; beatings, torture and rape (non-graphic) are common. The divide between the dark-haired, olive-skinned Astrean people and the pale-skinned, blonde-haired Kalovaxians is clearly along racial lines.<br /><br />BUT what can I say? It is also <b>an entertaining pageturner</b>. If you have room in your heart (and on your bookshelves) for another fantasy with princesses, evil rulers, rebellion and romance, then you could definitely do worse than this one.<br /><br />TW: graphic abuse and torture; rape (non-graphic); racism.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18129317990361328122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2359649200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2359649200" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2359649200?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2359649200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2977940069507837695">I hope you will not fall off your chair if I tell you that you have read this story before.<br/><br/>Maybe once, or twice, or a hundred of times, but you most certainly have. <br/><br/>Girl loses kingdom and family. Girl wants kingdom back and boy helps her. Girl manipulates her way surprisingly mainly into—instead of out of—trouble. <br/><br/>Nothing stands out. Not even the idea of multiple gods and goddesses and gems that hold power that can be used by and on people. There is the illusion of a world-building but it is jus</span>
  <span id="freeText2977940069507837695" style="display:none">I hope you will not fall off your chair if I tell you that you have read this story before.<br /><br />Maybe once, or twice, or a hundred of times, but you most certainly have. <br /><br />Girl loses kingdom and family. Girl wants kingdom back and boy helps her. Girl manipulates her way surprisingly mainly into—instead of out of—trouble. <br /><br />Nothing stands out. Not even the idea of multiple gods and goddesses and gems that hold power that can be used by and on people. There is the illusion of a world-building but it is just that… an illusion.<br /><br />So while you’ve read this story before, it’s true that you haven’t read it from Theo’s point of view. In the beginning, I was sure I would love it. After all, unlike most fantasy YA heroines, Theo *pretends* to be weak and a damsel in distress.<br /><br />The pretending entertained me. Except, when you think about it, whether she is aware of her own manipulative actions (like faking fear to let a guy protect her) or not, it remains that she isn’t acting all that differently from other fantasy YA heroines. <br /><br />I simply don’t care. Now I don’t mean that I want Theo to crumble and turn to real ashes, but if my powers of prediction are correct, that is not going to happen. Otherwise, there’s no story to tell, and so I don’t care to read the whole trilogy. (Pssst… I can also read hands, for a small fee.)<br /><br />Oh, wait, did I forget to mention that there’s a love triangle? Surprise! Now you’ve fallen completely, haven’t you? Well indeed there is. A very—wait for it—predictable and annoying one. <br /><br />What a waste of a really amazing cover (oh and potential). Though, was there potential to begin with? The only reason I read it is because I have a thing for princess stories or so I have claimed recently.<br /><br />But now I feel like a fraud. Grrr. I might have to rethink my preferences. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2977940069507837695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2177203620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177203620" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177203620?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177203620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer850879216755972858"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522782893i/25318527._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Penguin Random House in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My name is Theodosia Eirene Houzzara, Queen of Astrea, and I will endure this.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, I couldn’t put this down. This was such an addicting and captivating read. This was the first book of 2018 that I read in one day, which is saying something because this book is almost 450 pages. I was just so invested with the romance, the rebellion, and the betrayals, that I couldn’t stop turning the pages. <br/><br/><i>Ash Princess</i> is La</span>
  <span id="freeText850879216755972858" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522782893i/25318527._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Penguin Random House in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My name is Theodosia Eirene Houzzara, Queen of Astrea, and I will endure this.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, I couldn’t put this down. This was such an addicting and captivating read. This was the first book of 2018 that I read in one day, which is saying something because this book is almost 450 pages. I was just so invested with the romance, the rebellion, and the betrayals, that I couldn’t stop turning the pages. <br><br><i>Ash Princess</i> is Laura Sebastian's debut novel, which is a story about a girl named Theodosia (yeah, I’m going to be singing <i>Hamilton</i> all day after writing this review), whose ruling mother was murdered, and their land taken over by another kingdom when she was only six-years-old. the Kaiser allowed her to live, but only so that she could live among them, while they take everything she has ever known away. She is used as a reminder for her people that the Kaiser has enslaved, and when they do anything to rise up, Theodosia takes the punishment. Her back is incredible scarred from the whippings she has had to endure, but the Kaiser also inflicts so much mental and emotional abuse alongside the physical. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The last person who called me by my true name was my mother, with her dying breath.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The Kaiser conquered Theodosia’s land because there are caves that run beneath four major temples that her people worship (air, fire, water, earth). And gems come from those caves to give people magic, but they also give people with an affinity for the element(s) a lot of magic. The caves have so much magic inside them, that when Theodosia’s mother would rule, people would go down and stay in the caves, most dying, but some emerging and proving that they are worth the element the god and goddesses gave to them. Now that the Kaiser rules, he forces the slaves down there to mine, but most lose their minds after being around the power(s) for too long, and eventually lose their lives. <br><br>Theodosia’s only friend is a girl named Cress, whose father is the one who swiped the blade across her mother’s throat. Inside, Theodosia feels a constant battle about what she can do while feeling so absolutely helpless. Yet, Cress also lost her mother when she was very young, so an unconventional friendship grew from two girls both mourning the mothers they never got to know. I loved seeing their friendship develop and become what it was by the end of the book. But Theodosia is constantly reminded of all the things she lost alongside her mother, but she is forced to do the only thing she can: survive. That is, until one day a boy from her past comes and offers her a way out, and a way to maybe right a few wrongs that have happened to her people. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A life where a crown—gold or ash—doesn’t weigh heavy on my head.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>As I said above, this is a dark story about a girl who is forced to live among the people who ruined her life and killed her mother. <b>Trigger/Content Warnings</b> for racism, enslaving humans, abuse, torture, graphic beating, humiliation, captivation, gore, murder, death, loss of a loved one, bullying, talk of rape in the past, talk of animal murder in the past, sexual assault (unwanted touching), and rebellion/war themes. <br><br>The other thing I’d like to talk about is that the Kaiser and his people are white with light features, where Theodosia and her people have darker features and are said to have a “tawny” skin color. On top of the fact that this is a story about how one empire colonizes another, and puts the remaining population in chains and are force them to work (and die) in the mines harvesting gems. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Maybe his interest in me isn’t just about saving the damsel. Part of him also wants to be saved. If he’s stained by his father’s sins, then maybe I’m the only person who can absolve them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>My favorite thing about this book was easily the romance. Now, a lot of books have kind of vague, blurry, love triangles, but <i>Ash Princess</i> just has a blatant one, and I loved it. Theodosia is torn between her childhood friend and first love, Blaise, and a boy whose father has taken everything from her, Søren. It is legitimately friends to lovers and enemies to lovers and my shipper heart was so full of happiness. I personally like the enemies to lovers side of the triangle more, and I was falling off my bed, swooning so damn hard, during the last tunnel scene. Like, that is my romance kink, 100%, and if you’ve read this book you’ll know what scene I’m talking about. The romance in this is perfect, and I will read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358350872" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Smoke</a> at midnight upon release to see how these romances progress, because your girl is invested. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You could ask me for the ocean itself and I would find a way to give it to you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>So, you’re probably asking, “Melanie, why did you give it four stars if you enjoyed it this much and won’t stop gushing over it?” And that’s because, I’ll be honest, this story doesn’t bring anything new to the YA Fantasy world. If you read a lot of other reviews on Goodreads, you’re going to notice the same line of “this is nothing new” and it is true. A lot of reviewers are also comparing this to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546-red-queen?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758-an-ember-in-the-ashes" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a>, but I haven’t read either of those! Basically, this isn’t groundbreaking or even unique, but it’s super well written and crafted and it truly made for an un-put-downable read for me. <br><br>Overall, I truly loved and devoured this. This was easily the most addicting thing I’ve read in 2018 thus far, and I completely recommend it with my whole heart. Again, it might not be the most original thing, but that doesn’t make it not worthwhile. I loved the characters, the twists, the plot, the friendship, the perfect romances, the atmosphere, the writing, I loved it all. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“We are not defined by the things we do in order to survive.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="850879216755972858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2293868579" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2293868579" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2293868579?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Red Queen, Falling Kingdoms and Ruined, but this is BETTER</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=i-want-to-reread">i-want-to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=v-emotionally-moving">v-emotionally-moving</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=im-all-kinds-of-shook">im-all-kinds-of-shook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=bf">bf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2293868579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13706946847234702930">Edit: I accidentally read this as Ass Princess and that’s what I’ll always see when I look at this title.<br/><br/>This book is everything I wanted <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a> to be. 👏👏👏👏👏👏👏 What a fantastic debut. I loved this so much, I deadass want to reread it and experience all the feels all over again. It was just so addicting and I was unable to put this down!! I devoured this 400+ page book in two days. <br/><br/><i>Ash Princess</i> is a trope-filled book with a very common story line. Theodosia, or Theo, was six years old when she</span>
  <span id="freeText13706946847234702930" style="display:none">Edit: I accidentally read this as Ass Princess and that’s what I’ll always see when I look at this title.<br /><br />This book is everything I wanted <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a> to be. 👏👏👏👏👏👏👏 What a fantastic debut. I loved this so much, I deadass want to reread it and experience all the feels all over again. It was just so addicting and I was unable to put this down!! I devoured this 400+ page book in two days. <br /><br /><i>Ash Princess</i> is a trope-filled book with a very common story line. Theodosia, or Theo, was six years old when she witnessed her mother's (the queen) brutal murder and had her country conquered from her. In her country there are magical caves that run underneath the temples. For fire, air, earth and water. These are very sacred and only those who have proved themselves to the gods completely can go and get the magical gems. Now, Theo's people are forced to work as slaves in these mines and dig up the magical stones. <br /><br />For ten years she has been living under the Kaiser and his brutal rule, living quietly and trying to please him to survive. All of that ends when she's forced to kill <i>someone</i> and her childhood friend comes and offers her an escape and make things right for their people. She's filled with hate and determination to take back her kingdom and avenge her mother and people. <br /><br />Sounds so common, right? Hmm let's see, it sounds so much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26074185.Ruined__Ruined___1_" title="Ruined (Ruined, #1) by Amy Tintera" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruined</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a> (a lot of other YA books I can't think of right now), and the brutal world resembles a lot to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a>. But, I fucking loved this. In my opinion, this book was so much better than <i>Ruined</i> and <i>Red Queen</i>. <br /><br /><b>This world is so fucking brutal and violent,</b> a lot like <i>An Ember in ashes.</i> Theo is always whipped publicly whenever her people try to rebel. There is mention of rape, slaves are treated horrible, people are always being killed, like in <i>Falling Kingdoms</i>. But unlike, that book, <i>Ash Princess</i> isn't shit-ily written. People are being experimented on and a lot of gore and bloody things occur. There is horrible enslavement that Theo's people go through in the mines and there is vivid descriptions of the horrific things that go on there. <br /><br /><b>There is also a lot of racism that happens in this book.</b> The Kaiser and his people are white while Theo and her people have darker skin and described as "tawny." Theo's country is colonized and her people are enslaved and suffer through a lot of horrific shit. Theo is also mentally and physically abused, so <b>trigger warnings</b> for all that.<br /><br />Theo is a character that I really loved and sympathized with from the very beginning. Her life is horrible. Every day she has to be someone she's not and endure the humiliation and abuse from the Kaiser. She has no privacy of her own (literally, three guards called Shadows watch her 24/7, even when she's changing!!), cannot express her thoughts freely and lives in constant fear of the Kaiser. One wrong move and she'll piss the Kaiser off. Then when <i>that</i> happens and she learns of the horrors her people are going through, she snaps. <br /><br />She still has to pretend, but this time instead of fear, she's filled with hate. She's taking risks to meet with her people. She has to learn that the only way to win and survive is by hate and violence. She's also have an inner conflict with herself over her close friend in the castle and her growing feelings for the crown Prinz. She doesn't want to kill them, but if she is to take back her home, she's going to have to. <br /><br />I really understood her constant inner-battle. Her friend, Cress whose father slit Theo's mothers throat and whips her, is someone she's known for ten years in the castle. Cress helped her and stood up for her against bullies and has been nothing but kind to her. And now she's expected to kill her???? what.<br /><br /><b>Oh no, my guys, this has a LOVE TRIANGLE!!! [cue the groans of every person on the planet]</b> LISTEN, I know y'all hate love triangles and I DO TOO!! but this one is somehow bearable, even though it annoyed me a lot. Theo has feelings for the Prinz and her childhood friend, some dude, whose name I forgot, because I DON'T FUCKING SHIP THEM. He's a really good guy, but Prinz Soren and Theo all the way, bitch. Like, they're both good boys, but idk something about the Prinz, man.<br /><br />Okay, so this is fucking trope-filled and cliche as fuck so everyone's probably going to hate it but I loved it somehow so please read it!!! :( I'm joking, don't listen to me. Y'all probably gonna hate it LMAO. 😔<br /><br />I, personally, really loved this trope-y ass book and would recommend it!! Please give it a try!<br /><br /><br /><u>Pre-review:</u><br />I'm only reading it for the gorgeous cover. The plot sounds like 1000 other YA Fantasy books out there, but I still have hope that this'll be badass.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13706946847234702930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2179397883" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2179397883" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2179397883?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2179397883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17190592000815334020"><b>This was a pretty dark and politically twisty fantasy, and I was pretty sold!</b> It had powerful magic and intriguing world building and I am so there for this. <br/><br/><b> Seriously tho: world building!</b><br/>It actually takes time to show us languages and cultures and there were a lot of "fantasy" words flying about, but I didn't get confused. I felt really sucked into the world after only a few chapters. Plus it had a lot of fantastic details so everything seemed super vivid!<br/><br/><b> It has a lot of "prettiness" in it to</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17190592000815334020" style="display:none"><b>This was a pretty dark and politically twisty fantasy, and I was pretty sold!</b> It had powerful magic and intriguing world building and I am so there for this. <br /><br /><b> Seriously tho: world building!</b><br />It actually takes time to show us languages and cultures and there were a lot of "fantasy" words flying about, but I didn't get confused. I felt really sucked into the world after only a few chapters. Plus it had a lot of fantastic details so everything seemed super vivid!<br /><br /><b> It has a lot of "prettiness" in it to balance the horror of the conquerors.</b><br />It's absolutely about a conquered nation, and Theo is basically a trophy, tortured daily for the crimes of her people but kept alive despite the horror she has to go through. So she's like lavished in pretty dresses and wears pretty makeup and goes to banquets and has books. Her BFF is one the daughter of a very powerful dude and she's all pretty and light and flippant. But then in the background you have the conquered people being murdered and enslaved in mines and Theo's being whipped if they rebel. It was a brutal and visual contrast.<br /><br /><b> This one had such a stunning world and so much potential for sequels.<b> It's about wicked conquerors and the glitter and jewels people will pile on top of festering poison and murders and I was definitely intrigued.</b></b></span>

<div id="review_2747455327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2747455327" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2747455327?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/40737383-ash-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2018-publication">2018-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=rh">rh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2747455327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10717714388205543387"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>There's no denying:<br/><br/>--This could have been more intricately plotted.<br/>--The characters could have been more developed.<br/>--Some of the violence, because there are repeated beatings, could have been written with more emotional and physical impact <br/>--There is a half-hearted triangle. (sorta? Maybe more of a red herring.)<br/>--After 400+ pages, I'm still not entirely sure how all the magic works. <br/><br/>And yet...I enjoyed it! It doesn't hurt that the book starts off with a doozy of an act, one that clearly</span>
  <span id="freeText10717714388205543387" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />There's no denying:<br /><br />--This could have been more intricately plotted.<br />--The characters could have been more developed.<br />--Some of the violence, because there are repeated beatings, could have been written with more emotional and physical impact <br />--There is a half-hearted triangle. (sorta? Maybe more of a red herring.)<br />--After 400+ pages, I'm still not entirely sure how all the magic works. <br /><br />And yet...I enjoyed it! It doesn't hurt that the book starts off with a doozy of an act, one that clearly shows you the girl you are dealing with. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Theodosia kills her own father as an act of mercy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I KNOW. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The measured way Theodosia makes decisions and feels about her relationships makes me like her a lot, particularly in how she deals with her parents and her old Astrean friends, and maybe above all, in the tenuous bonds she's formed with the Kalovaxians who enslaved her people. The country is at war, and Theodosia is at war with herself over how she feels about her friend Cress. But she is clear-eyed about Cress loving her in return as she would a favored pet, and about her romance with Soren being untrustworthy, because he doesn't truly know her. I also like that the book is honest about how a person in Theodosia's position would use whatever means she has, including her feminine wiles, to gain advantage and to deceive, without making her lose integrity or the reader's trust.<br /><br />I found this to be compulsively readable and I was eager to get back the audio version every time I took a break. Saskia Maarleveld's narration also sounds very much like Eva Green as Vesper Lynde in parts, which is incredibly seductive to listen to. She gives each character subtle inflections and shading, and her performance was highly enjoyable to me.<br /><br />If you swooned over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> as a whole or responded with excitement to the action elements of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30375703.The_Valiant__The_Valiant___1_" title="The Valiant (The Valiant, #1) by Lesley Livingston" rel="nofollow noopener">The Valiant</a> (or maybe even the action parts of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27774758.An_Ember_in_the_Ashes__An_Ember_in_the_Ashes___1_" title="An Ember in the Ashes (An Ember in the Ashes, #1) by Sabaa Tahir" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember in the Ashes</a>), this is definitely worth a read. <br /><br /><i>An audio review copy was provided by the publisher.</i> <br /><br />Screw it, I'm rounding up because I enjoyed it.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2325231650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1433762116502844679">EVERYONE NEEDS TO READ THIS BOOK. IT IS PHENOMENAL. <br/><br/>Theo is so strong, and actually a normal character who relates to things normally which i loved, felt i could relate to her a little better. Magic, kings, war and spying. i could barely put it down! I'm so excited for the sequel already and i can't believe i have to wait another year!<br/><br/>And I know it had a love triangle, but it was so believable for me.<br/><br/>And the struggle, omg. And the humiliation. Jesus Christ. <br/><br/>Theo reminds me a little of Tris from </span>
  <span id="freeText1433762116502844679" style="display:none">EVERYONE NEEDS TO READ THIS BOOK. IT IS PHENOMENAL. <br /><br />Theo is so strong, and actually a normal character who relates to things normally which i loved, felt i could relate to her a little better. Magic, kings, war and spying. i could barely put it down! I'm so excited for the sequel already and i can't believe i have to wait another year!<br /><br />And I know it had a love triangle, but it was so believable for me.<br /><br />And the struggle, omg. And the humiliation. Jesus Christ. <br /><br />Theo reminds me a little of Tris from divergent but she is such a strong young woman.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1433762116502844679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2325568271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325568271" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2325568271?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2325568271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4316832687686002012">So earlier this year I took a trip to the south of France, notably the Périgord, which is filled with lovely relaxed people with sun-kissed skin and floaty skirts, a nice contrast to my jumpy pasty ass (I was in the middle of an existential crisis and musing over whether or not to quit my job and become a starving artist, and The Results May Surprise You!). <br/><br/>While I was there I went to this antiques shop filled with retro fridges and dusty comics and amazing vinyl albums from the 80's, from <i>befor</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4316832687686002012" style="display:none">So earlier this year I took a trip to the south of France, notably the Périgord, which is filled with lovely relaxed people with sun-kissed skin and floaty skirts, a nice contrast to my jumpy pasty ass (I was in the middle of an existential crisis and musing over whether or not to quit my job and become a starving artist, and The Results May Surprise You!). <br /><br />While I was there I went to this antiques shop filled with retro fridges and dusty comics and amazing vinyl albums from the 80's, from <i>before I was even born, my dudes</i>, which makes me look like a foetus or whatever. Anyway, I was agonising over this fucking incredible standing lamp with an old aged leather lampshade, teeth clenched over the €150 price tag, but... Okay. Let me paint you a picture, here. The lamp was about my height, and the lampshade was at the top, of course, but it was balanced on this handmade ye olde globe, and the globe was being held up by a faux-gold almost-life-sized sculpture of Atlas. It was like a blend of everything I love: good light to read by, inaccurate old-timey maps, and Greek mythology. I was just standing over this lamp, a thread of drool wetting the front of my sweaty t-shirt (it was upwards of thirty degrees all week, and that's not safe for a pale Celtic weirdo like me), trying not to reach into my purse for my credit card. <br /><br />Eventually, I talked myself out of it. Okay, that's a lie. I tore myself away from it, like one might tear a glob of gum from their hair, because that lamp would look so fucking good in my flat, next to the K-2SO figurine and the red thread pinned into the plasterboard and the giant snail in the tank in the living room. I kept cursing it, cursing how poor I am, until I came across a cardboard box full of - no, not false nails or chicken feet. No. It was full of carnivale masks. <br /><br />They weren't the lamp, but they were pretty cool. I dithered between two of them, one with a big velvet ruff and covered in bells, and another smaller one with a salty little smirk on her face. I eventually chose the one with the bells, and it was only like €15, which was... acceptable. Jesus Christ, it wasn't the damn lamp, but it would do. I liked it. <br /><br />It took me a while to get the mask home, because there wasn't enough room in my luggage, but some weeks later I was balancing on the back of the ugly pink armchair, one eye on the TV watching <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/Kurzgesagt" rel="nofollow noopener">Kurzgesagt</a> and trying not to press a push pin through my finger. Then the mask was up, and it looks cool, and but le sigh. I'll never forget about the lamp. It will live on in my heart forever. <br /><br />So here's the thing. When you read this next part, you'll probably envision me tapping away at my crumb-filled 2012 MacBook next to my giant snail, surrounded by crystals and dusty ornaments and sporting a tin-foil hat, and save for the tin-foil hat, you're not wrong. The point is that on the Ghoul Boys scale, I'm not a Boogara, but nor am I a Shaniac. I'm sort of in the middle, and I have my own theories, and all I'm saying is HEAR ME OUT. <br /><br />It started on the day that the mask arrived in my home. On that day, I experienced my very first lucid dream. It was one of the most terrifying things I've ever fucking witnessed and someday, if anyone's interested, I'll talk about it. I took notes down on my phone the second I woke up, but I needn't have bothered: I remember the dream so vividly, and I also remember the absolutely paralysing fear that I experienced. I know it was a lucid dream, and within the dream I was aware that I was dreaming; I said the words to myself inside my head: <i>I am in a dream</i>. But it was baffling, visceral, and indescribably frightening. I woke up feeling like I had already lived through a day. The full story is for another time but that's still notable. <br /><br />Something changed when the mask went up on the wall. I was sitting in the living room, watching <i>Friends</i> and drawing with my crusty old tablet, and I heard the shoeboxes in my bedroom stir, like they were being shuffled around. My flat is fairly small, and the front door opens out to a short hallway with the bedroom to the left and the living room to the right; the noise was therefore loud enough for me to hear over my roaring laughter at the timeless joy of everyone's favourite 90's sitcom and two (albeit open) doors. An important thing to note here is that there are only two shoeboxes and they're fairly big, so it's not easy for them to topple. <br /><br />I texted my sister about this, and she seemed spooked. At the time, surprisingly, I wasn't worried. I also woke up the morning after the shoebox incident with blinding lateral foot pain that was so bad I couldn't walk, though I had run 4km the day prior to that so I put it down to overexercise. Though I should mention that I had completed that same 4km run many times before with no trouble and had also been exercising quite diligently for weeks before that, so... Make of it what you will. <br /><br />A couple of days later I was lying in bed at about 9am* scrolling through Tumblr, and I heard a funny clattering in the bathroom, like something being knocked by an elbow. Now, my bathroom is stacked absolutely full of useless crap, including but not limited to empty toothpaste boxes, empty shampoo bottles, face masks, 40 vol bleach bottles, a dying orchid, and like eight pairs of sunglasses (???) so it's easy to turn around and knock stuff over. I glanced at the door, then went back to scrolling on Tumblr. Whatever, dude. <br /><br />*Don't hate me, but I tend to write off any paranormal experiences that start with "I had just woken up". Sleep messes with your mind, guys. Stuff like false awakening and sleep paralysis can seriously dick around with your perception of reality. I've experienced false awakening before and later discovered after some extensive research that what I thought was a crazy paranormal experience was just my brain tricking me into thinking I had three arms. I'm always open to suggestion but I tend to take anything that happens just after waking up from REM sleep with a big, big pinch of salt. What makes me pause on this is that I woke up at 8am and had been solidly awake but lying in bed for about an hour, scrolling through social media, when this happened. <br /><br />Last night, just after I had settled down to sleep, I heard what sounded like the fridge door closing. This gave me pause, because before I go to bed I obsessively check the locks on the door, check to make sure the sockets are off at the wall, check to make sure the taps are off, and check to make sure the fridge and freezer are shut. This is a ritual, because if I haven't double, and sometimes triple, checked these things then I lie awake all night getting anxious about it. I did these checks, of course, and then the fridge door shut. Okay. <br /><br />My flat has been sweltering all summer. It's still warm outside. My flat is now cold. Throughout the entire summer, whenever I opened a window, flies and bees and wasps always buzzed inside and annoyed the crap out of me. The windows have been open every day since the mask entered my home and I have not seen a single bug. There are creaks and small movements in the night. I wake every now and again at between 3 and 5am, though I usually sleep like a corpse. <br /><br />Am I imagining it? Probably. But I've seen and heard enough creepy shit in my life to believe that there's more out there than what we can see. And I had prepared, throughout my years, for something of this ilk to happen to me - I had imagined what it might be to live alone and wonder if maybe I wasn't really as alone as I thought. Every time I pictured it, I saw myself terrified and unable to sleep and back in my old childhood home where I could not shake the feeling of being watched. <br /><br />But the thing is that I just honestly don't give a damn. I'm stressed and trying to break into publishing is a fucking disaster and I'm just, like, okay. Whatever. You can haunt my home if you want to, as long as you stay in your corner and I stay in mine. Just don't break anything and we're cool. I can sit at my weird hoofed coffee table and write and this thing, whatever it is, if it even exists, can pulse away inside that mask that feels like it's staring at me, as long as it doesn't scare my friends or pick at the wallpaper. It's cool. I'm fine with it. Let's just both move on with our lives and coexist. <br /><br />You were wondering where the book comes in, right?<br /><br />I feel the same way about this book as I do about the mask. The book's very pretty, but its contents aren't to my taste. That said, I don't harbour any ill feeling towards it. Some years ago I'd have hissed and spat at this book for being so simplistic and depressing and at the same time boring and expected (elemental magic? Really? Come on. It's 20gayteen) but now, as a grown woman, I'm fine with it. It's whatever. It was very, very standard YA fare and I doubt I'll remember it in 6 weeks' time. It'll sit on my book...shelf, no, not a shelf, just a stack on the floor, and as long as it doesn't fall and crush my toe or anything, then it can do its thing and I'll do mine. I can move on from it and forget about it and lament nothing about my time with it. It was blah and thinner than rice paper but I really can't force myself to care. <br /><br />Maybe I should be more pissed off about the book than the ghost, but the ghost cost €15 and the book only set me back like £7.99. The ghost is a better investment, probably, but given the barren fucking wasteland that is my life right now, I'd say they're both equally irrelevant. The only thing I'm cheesed about is the collective £21.35 I paid for a very low-key haunting and a long eye roll. Thanks, Brexit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4316832687686002012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2212985933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2212985933" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212985933?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36102322-ash-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36817401-carrie?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212985933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13500947717124022167">Ash Princess by Laura Sebastian is the first book in the young adult fantasy series, Ash Princess Trilogy. This is one that is on the darker side with violence, abuse, slavery and a hint of rape so beware to those with issues with these triggers. There is also a hint of a love triangle involved with the main character, a boy from her past and the son (prince) of her captor.<br/><br/>The story begins as we meet Theodosia Eirene Houzzara who by all rights should be the Queen of Astrea. However ten years bef</span>
  <span id="freeText13500947717124022167" style="display:none">Ash Princess by Laura Sebastian is the first book in the young adult fantasy series, Ash Princess Trilogy. This is one that is on the darker side with violence, abuse, slavery and a hint of rape so beware to those with issues with these triggers. There is also a hint of a love triangle involved with the main character, a boy from her past and the son (prince) of her captor.<br /><br />The story begins as we meet Theodosia Eirene Houzzara who by all rights should be the Queen of Astrea. However ten years before Theodosia’s people were overthrown and her mother the queen was killed in front of her. Since that day she has done whatever she can to stay alive despite the torture she’s endured. <br /><br />When Theodosia’s father who once was a guard in her kingdom is brought into the court for “trial” and sentenced to death at her own hand it sparks something in the fallen princess. She knows that many of her people have died but even if it costs her own life she must do what she can to regain her throne.<br /><br />I suppose the first thing to say about this one would be that no, it isn’t a highly original tale but more of one done before. However, when they mention a series like Red Queen in comparison I was hesitant to even try this one because of finding that one so slow and dare I say boring. Ash Princess may have hints of the same type of young adult fantasy read as others before it but it was strangely enjoying to me regardless and I felt myself get caught up in the story as it went along.<br /><br />The writing in here seemed to flow rather easily for such a dark tale and had a compelling feel to it I’ve missed in other books of this type. The stage has been set in this first book and with a somewhat cliffhanger type of ending it seems there are sure to be some big developments to come with the plot so yes, I will definitely continue the series on to see how it goes from here.<br /><br />I received an advance copy from the publisher via NetGalley.<br /><br />For more reviews please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13500947717124022167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2424789827" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2424789827" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2424789827?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2424789827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5712391060168104427"><b>--2.5 stars--</b><br/><br/>This book was... fine. It wasn't horrible, it wasn't particularly great, it was just okay. It reads like literally any YA fantasy book you've ever read. If you're looking for something groundbreaking or innovative, then there's nothing to see here. It felt like the author had a YA Fantasy 101 handbook to refer to during the writing process. Like, there isn't a single thing I can think of about this book that gives it its own identity. Feels like it was made by a machine that figured</span>
  <span id="freeText5712391060168104427" style="display:none"><b>--2.5 stars--</b><br /><br />This book was... fine. It wasn't horrible, it wasn't particularly great, it was just okay. It reads like literally any YA fantasy book you've ever read. If you're looking for something groundbreaking or innovative, then there's nothing to see here. It felt like the author had a YA Fantasy 101 handbook to refer to during the writing process. Like, there isn't a single thing I can think of about this book that gives it its own identity. Feels like it was made by a machine that figured out the algorithm to create the perfect cookie cutter YA fantasy novel, marketable and safe.<br /><br />I find it hard to believe that this is a 2018 release. This book would've been somewhat interesting if it was released, like, 2013 or something. Are we really still doing torn-between-two-guys love triangles in this day and age? Like, come on. Next thing you know, they're gonna be revealed to be brothers or some shit. I know in this book's case that's literally impossible, since the two love interests are of different ethnicities, but hey, it's YA. The two guys always end up miraculously being brothers lol.<br /><br />Honestly I really wanted to DNF this book but I powered through it cause I wanted to see how it would end. I wanted to see if this book had <i>something</i> that would surprise me, but nope. Nothing. I'd suggest skipping this if you're looking for something new and refreshing. If you wanna read more of the same, though, look no further. This is about as basic as it gets.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5712391060168104427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2420176818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420176818" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420176818?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420176818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15974122086597143757"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>In YA, everyone piles onto the bandwagon of the latest trends. A few years ago it was dystopian fiction but now we've a glut of fantasy on our hands. As someone who loves fantasy, this should be a good thing, but the YA machine keeps churning out subpar, derivative works that are less good world-building and action-heavy plots than wallpaper fantasy settings for tepid romance.<br/><br/><br/><br/>In this regard, ASH PRINCESS is no exception.<br/><br/><br/><br/>I'm really annoye</span>
  <span id="freeText15974122086597143757" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>In YA, everyone piles onto the bandwagon of the latest trends. A few years ago it was dystopian fiction but now we've a glut of fantasy on our hands. As someone who loves fantasy, this should be a good thing, but the YA machine keeps churning out subpar, derivative works that are less good world-building and action-heavy plots than wallpaper fantasy settings for tepid romance.<br><br><br><br>In this regard, ASH PRINCESS is no exception.<br><br><br><br>I'm really annoyed about that because the book started out really good. Theodosia is the ex-princess of a country that has been invaded by conquerors. All of her people are slaves but for some reason they keep her around as a court mockery, forcing her to wear an ash crown that stains her clothes, while mocking her and subjecting her to public beatings for her people's infractions.<br><br><br><br>Obviously this means that when rebellion inevitably stirs from resentment about the genocide and the slavery and the torture, Theodosia is going to be chosen as the figurehead. And her jaded bitterness in the beginning gave me hope that despite the stupid names for everything (kaiser and prinz, seriously? why German names if it's not a German-inspired country? did you just choose foreign words for ruler than sounded "exotic"), I was hoping that this would be a fantasy novel cast in the mold of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1647791187" rel="nofollow noopener">THE WINNER'S CURSE</a>, my ultimate favorite.<br><br><br><br>The problem occurs when Theodosia is supposed to seduce the - cringe- "prinz," Soren, in order to get information about his people and their future plans for conquering before killing him. She drops that jaded bitterness right quick and Bella Swans it up, despairing about how much it'll hurt to kill such a cute boy when she betrays him, conveniently forgetting about all her people dying in slave mines. Similar whining occurs when she realizes she may have to kill her best friend, the daughter of the evil kaiser's closest adviser and the man who whips her before everyone to punish her.<br><br><br><br>Great choice in friends.<br><br><br><br>The other side of the love triangle is Blaise, one of her own people who is involved with the revolution. She's known him since childhood, although she never mentions him until he shows up on the scene bringing tidings of revolution. Go figure. I didn't really care for him, but after I found out that Prinz Soren is a <b>cat murderer</b>, he could never redeem himself for me. I guess I don't find wishy-washy heroes who can't stand up to their tyrant fathers and kill small animals attractive?<br><br><br><br>Theodosia does, though. She hardly bats an eye at the cat murdering bit. <br><br><br><br>I'm giving this 2.5 stars because it was entertaining and the concept of elemental "Spiritgems" giving people powers over fire, air, water, and earth kind of sounded like something straight out of one of those JRPGs, specifically the <i>Mana </i>series (in fact, if you haven't watched it already, I recommend that you check out CollegeHumor's "<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IptvSQY9Qa8" rel="nofollow noopener">Every JRPG Ever</a>." It's weirdly appropriate for this book). The world really should have been developed more, and Theodosia should have had more of a spine (and less of an, "oh, woe is me! I'm in love with <i>two </i>boys!" attitude). You know a heroine's in hot water when your sympathies lie with the people telling her to get her act together and not with the heroine herself. Like, "Yeah, get your act together! You're an effing princess! Stop dallying around!" But then again, this is YA fantasy and at this point, I pretty much come in expecting to be disappointed.<br><br><br><br><i>Thanks to Netgalley/the publisher for the review copy!</i> <br><br><br><br>2.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="15974122086597143757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2200171286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2200171286" />
    <a title="Candace Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson"><img alt="Candace Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530157383p2/33995641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2200171286?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace Robinson" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson">Candace Robinson</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2200171286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15576695737816365423">I'm just going to open up and say this book is just a jumbo of every other YA fantasy book thrown together, especially Ruined by Amy Tintera, which is a book that I loved. It also had Red Queen vibes. I think if this would have been my first YA fantasy book, I would have probably liked it a lot more. Also, throw in my most hated trope, sort of a weird love triangle, and you already have me annoyed. Actually, I'm not even sure if it was a triangle, but there were multiple kisses going on. <br/><br/>Another</span>
  <span id="freeText15576695737816365423" style="display:none">I'm just going to open up and say this book is just a jumbo of every other YA fantasy book thrown together, especially Ruined by Amy Tintera, which is a book that I loved. It also had Red Queen vibes. I think if this would have been my first YA fantasy book, I would have probably liked it a lot more. Also, throw in my most hated trope, sort of a weird love triangle, and you already have me annoyed. Actually, I'm not even sure if it was a triangle, but there were multiple kisses going on. <br /><br />Another thing that bothers me is when a character is annoying and takes herself too seriously. Theo/Thora just kept on saying my people this, and I'm the queen that. She also has all these intense memories from when she was seven or younger. I feel like I can barely remember yesterday, let alone when I was five.<br /><br />What was good is that the writing was really well done, and if some of the trope things would have been removed (like girl pretending she likes a guy to betray/kill him, but she really likes him) it would have been a lot better. I just need something more fresh/different. However, I would still read the next book to see what happens next...</span>
  <a data-text-id="15576695737816365423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
